<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c0b98dcb-e89d-4141-9459-11a3cc102439'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14247965872852160445">LAPD cop Scott James is not doing so well. Eight months ago, a shocking nighttime assault by unidentified men killed his partner Stephanie, nearly killed him, and left him enraged, ashamed, and ready to explode.   <span id="freeText14247965872852160445" style="display:none">LAPD cop Scott James is not doing so well. Eight months ago, a shocking nighttime assault by unidentified men killed his partner Stephanie, nearly killed him, and left him enraged, ashamed, and ready to explode. He is unfit for duty...until he meets his new partner.<br /><br />Maggie is not doing so well, either. A German shepherd who survived three tours in Iraq and Afghanistan sniffing explosives before losing her handler to an IED, her PTSD is as bad as Scott's.<br /><br />They are each other's last chance. Shunned and shunted to the side, they set out to investigate the one case that no one wants them to touch: the identity of the men who murdered Stephanie. What they begin to find is nothing like what Scott has been told, and the journey will take them both through the darkest moments of their own personal hells. Whether they will make it out again, no one can say.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I am a huge fan of Michael Connelly's series of Harry Bosch. David Baldacci has written dozens also of various series, my favorite being the camel clu<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I am a huge fan of Michael Connelly's series of Harry Bosch. David Baldacci has written dozens also of various series, my favorite being the camel club. <br /><br />If you like stories about detective work and PTSD, read the Ian Rutledge series by Charles Todd. Important to start at the beginning of both the Harry Bosch above and Ian Rutledge as their characters evolve with time. Enjoy <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_513131453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513131453" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513131453?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=5-0">5-0</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513131453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4130251073620987739">My mother is the office manager for a small city’s police department and several years ago I visited her at work, and she introduced me around the station. The K9 came in with his handler, and the dog ran up to my mom for a happy hello. He noticed me and immediately went into a Who-The-Hell-Is-In-My-Office mode. The officer gave him the ‘Be cool.’ command, and the dog was instantly friendly. After a quick sniff to make sure I wasn’t carrying drugs or explosives (Luckily, I had locked them all in</span>
  <span id="freeText4130251073620987739" style="display:none">My mother is the office manager for a small city’s police department and several years ago I visited her at work, and she introduced me around the station. The K9 came in with his handler, and the dog ran up to my mom for a happy hello. He noticed me and immediately went into a Who-The-Hell-Is-In-My-Office mode. The officer gave him the ‘Be cool.’ command, and the dog was instantly friendly. After a quick sniff to make sure I wasn’t carrying drugs or explosives (Luckily, I had locked them all in the trunk.), the dog sat in front of me so I could pet him. <br /><br />The cop was standing right beside him, and my mom said, “Just don’t grab the officer’s sleeve or arm or anything.” <br /><br />I laughed a bit thinking she was joking. <br /><br />“No, she’s serious. We’re so close that he’d get a couple of good bites in before I could pull him off if you touched me,” the cop said gravely.<br /><br />I looked down at the dog who nodded as if to say, “Yes, I am enjoying the way you’re scratching my ears but if you touch my guy, I am gonna mess you up.”<br /><br />Needless to say, I was very careful not to touch the cop. <br /><br />So that's my police dog story. Here's one from Robert Crais:<br /><br />LAPD officer Scott James had the bad luck to get caught up in firefight with a group of masked man that killed his partner Stephanie and severely wounded him. Months later, Scott is hiding the extent of his physical injuries that should have gotten him an early retirement. He's also suffering from a whopping case of PTSD and survivor’s guilt. He has asked to be a K9 officer not because he really loves dogs, but because he doesn’t want to deal with a human partner.<br /><br />German shepherd Maggie was a Marine who sniffed out IED’s, but she was wounded in an ambush that killed her beloved handler. Heartbroken at the loss of her master and suffering from the dog form of PTSD, Maggie is about to be kicked out of the LAPD’s K9 program for being too surly and gun shy to be of any use. When Scott hears Maggie’s story, it strikes a chord, and he’ll need a good partner since he’s still determined to help track down Stephanie’s killers.<br /><br />Robert Crais is good at writing damaged people. Whether it’s an ugly childhood like Elvis Cole and Joe Pike both went through or a cop left shattered by a traumatic injury like Carol Starkey in <i>Demolition Angel</i> or a police negotiator who loses his nerve after one bad day like in <i>Hostage</i>, Crais always makes you feel their pain. He includes empathy for suffering that is strangely lacking in a lot of crime fiction.<br /><br />So the story of Scott and Maggie is right in his wheelhouse with the two damaged creatures forming a bond. You can’t help but like these two, and Crais is careful not to overdo it since it’d be really easy to play the injured dog card and ride it right to the best seller list. As always, he put in the effort to give a quality crime story and not just lean on the tragic parts too much.<br /><br />However, this isn’t the best Robert Crais I’ve read. That’s kind of damning it with faint praise though. While I liked it a lot, it didn’t have quite the emotional heft of some of the recent Elvis Cole books I’ve read, and the mystery/action stuff wasn’t as relentless as in <i>Hostage</i>. But it’s still good, and Crais’s good is more than a lot of writer’s best. <br /><br />Plus, you know, it’s got a dog in it. How can you not like that?<br /><br />Three stars with a smiley face using the new Dan rating’s scale.<br /><br />Also posted at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2013/04/a-boy-and-his-dog.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4130251073620987739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9095105756471582414">Amazon-Audible- Daily Special: Narrated by MacLeod Andre<br/><br/>I had never heard of this author - nor had I read any reviews. I liked the ‘sample’ - downloaded it and began listening right away. <br/><br/>Maggie is one of the greatest characters in this detective crime novel. Maggie is a German Shepherd, weighing eighty-five pounds. Oh my gosh ... I love her! <br/><br/>At the start we meet Maggie and her partner Pete Gibbs. They are both in the marines. While in Afghanistan, their unit is attacked by enemy fire. Pete and </span>
  <span id="freeText9095105756471582414" style="display:none">Amazon-Audible- Daily Special: Narrated by MacLeod Andre<br /><br />I had never heard of this author - nor had I read any reviews. I liked the ‘sample’ - downloaded it and began listening right away. <br /><br />Maggie is one of the greatest characters in this detective crime novel. Maggie is a German Shepherd, weighing eighty-five pounds. Oh my gosh ... I love her! <br /><br />At the start we meet Maggie and her partner Pete Gibbs. They are both in the marines. While in Afghanistan, their unit is attacked by enemy fire. Pete and Maggie were a strong team - madly in love and devoted to each other —but when Pete is killed - PETE WAS GREAT TOO... I was sad to see him leave this story so soon. ( I get attached fast to my little friends in the novels I read). <br />Maggie physically insured.....( geeeee, lots of sadness at the start of this book)...<br />It’s clear Maggie’s heartbroken wound is much more serious than her physical ones. <br />Maggie is diagnosed with PTSD. I was so emotionally invested in this story. I’m thinking....”WHO IS THIS AUTHOR?” “I’m enjoying storytime!!!<br /><br />Scott James, like Maggie, has also been physically wounded. Scott’s a patrolman for the Los Angeles Police Department - LAPD. Scott was shot several times one evening when he and his partner, Stephanie Anders was killed. Things happened fast. One minute Scott and Stephanie were expressing appreciation for each other’s partnership and looking for a noodle house, when suddenly they were smack in the middle of a shooting escapade. It was horrific— Scott couldn’t save Stephanie. He loss consciousness from the gun shots and woke up 9 months later in a hospital. <br /><br />The reader can already see that Scott, with PTSD, and Maggie with PTSD, are going to become partners, buddies, and soul mates, — but we don’t care about the obvious predictability because - we’re happy they are bonding: period! Little by little we see Maggie and Scott growing as close as Maggie once was with Pete. They even compare battle wound scars with each other —-Maggie’s fur has not fully grown back to cover her scar and Scott’s scars are still pretty pronounced. <br />I felt like jumping into the ‘scar-game’ and showing them mine, too. <br /><br />The bonding between Scott &amp; Maggie is a treasure....but they have a job to do together too ....the mystery/ suspense unfolds at a great pace —- There are chapters written from Maggie’s point of view- a dog’s perspective- and it’s very believable- not at all cheezy. <br /><br />Pure enjoyment- a nice surprise! My only question is.... what Robert Crais book should I read for my next selection? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9095105756471582414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2177230384394256708"><b>Best Dog Book Ever!</b><br/><br/>Perhaps you'll start this book, as I did, by wishing it had been Elvis Cole #14 and/or Joe Pike #5. But you will definitely finish it cheering and hoping that it is actually Scott & Maggie #1!<br/><br/>This was a great new read from Robert Crais with a cast of new characters (although the hyper sex-driven SID criminalist John Chen from the Cole/Pike books makes a cameo appearance in his usual sleazy style) centring around two post-traumatic stress syndrome damaged survivors trying to ma</span>
  <span id="freeText2177230384394256708" style="display:none"><b>Best Dog Book Ever!</b><br /><br />Perhaps you'll start this book, as I did, by wishing it had been Elvis Cole #14 and/or Joe Pike #5. But you will definitely finish it cheering and hoping that it is actually Scott &amp; Maggie #1!<br /><br />This was a great new read from Robert Crais with a cast of new characters (although the hyper sex-driven SID criminalist John Chen from the Cole/Pike books makes a cameo appearance in his usual sleazy style) centring around two post-traumatic stress syndrome damaged survivors trying to make a go of it again. The trick is, one of them is a dog!<br /><br />This isn't one of those anthropomorphic animal books where the dog is assigned all sorts of unlikely human-like thoughts. Maggie the german shepherd comes across as a real dog with dog-like characteristics and no more than that, but those traits are more than enough to make you love her.<br /><br />And by the end you will be looking at your closest loved ones (either two or four-legged) and smiling and thinking to yourself: "Pack!"<br /><br />Highly recommended!<br /><br /><b>August 2017 Update</b><br />p.s. If you loved "Suspect," check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32620357.The_Right_Side" title="The Right Side by Spencer Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Right Side</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1932450.Spencer_Quinn" title="Spencer Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Spencer Quinn</a>. It's not like the Chet &amp; Bernie novels, but is grittier and harder edged. No more spoilers here.</span>

    <a title="O&#39;Dell Isaac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3028989-o-dell-isaac"><img alt="O&#39;Dell Isaac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263627885p2/3028989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536224154?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="O&#39;Dell Isaac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="O&#39;Dell Isaac" href="/user/show/3028989-o-dell-isaac">O&#39;Dell Isaac</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536224154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15308485352354931901">I'm a big fan of Robert Crais' Elvis Cole series (and the Joe Pike spinoff series), but I must admit I have been less of a fan of his stand-alone fiction. This is not a knock on Crais as a writer; it's more about my own tendency to form attachments to series characters. So when Suspect came out and I realized it was a stand-alone, I was less than enthused. But in my desperation for something new to read, I reluctantly picked it up.<br/><br/>It turned out to be one of Crais' best novels.<br/><br/>LAPD officer Scott </span>
  <span id="freeText15308485352354931901" style="display:none">I'm a big fan of Robert Crais' Elvis Cole series (and the Joe Pike spinoff series), but I must admit I have been less of a fan of his stand-alone fiction. This is not a knock on Crais as a writer; it's more about my own tendency to form attachments to series characters. So when Suspect came out and I realized it was a stand-alone, I was less than enthused. But in my desperation for something new to read, I reluctantly picked it up.<br /><br />It turned out to be one of Crais' best novels.<br /><br />LAPD officer Scott James is in bad shape, still dealing with the physical and mental wounds from an ambush shooting that left his partner dead. Maggie, a military working dog, is in equally bad shape, rehabbing from an IED/sniper attack that left her bullet-torn and her handler dead. Man and dog begin to form an alliance as they endeavor to heal themselves and each other, while Scott searches for the criminals who murdered his partner.<br /><br />If you are a fan of mysteries -- or a fan of dogs -- you can't miss with Suspect. It moves along at a brisk pace, provides a slam-bang climax, and may even wring a tear or two out of you.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer515307330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14737888820935277475"><br/>In this first book in the 'Scott James and Maggie' series, the police officer and his K-9 dog do their initial training and investigate a crime. <br/><br/>*****<br/><br/>Police Officer Scott James is badly injured and his partner is killed when they inadvertently stumble into a heist on a Los Angeles street. Elsewhere, Maggie, a German Shepherd "Marine dog" is shot and injured while sniffing for explosives in Afghanistan. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584186946i/29105833.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Months later, after they heal, Scott and Maggie come together in the K-9 (cop/dog) unit of the</span>
  <span id="freeText14737888820935277475" style="display:none"><br>In this first book in the 'Scott James and Maggie' series, the police officer and his K-9 dog do their initial training and investigate a crime. <br><br>*****<br><br>Police Officer Scott James is badly injured and his partner is killed when they inadvertently stumble into a heist on a Los Angeles street. Elsewhere, Maggie, a German Shepherd "Marine dog" is shot and injured while sniffing for explosives in Afghanistan. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584186946i/29105833.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Months later, after they heal, Scott and Maggie come together in the K-9 (cop/dog) unit of the Los Angeles police department. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584186946i/29105835.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Scott and Maggie train and bond under the tutelage of veteran handler Sgt. Dominick Leland. The bonding of man and dog is an important, touching, sometimes humorous part of the book as love and loyalty grows between the pair. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584187344i/29105856.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meanwhile Scott continues to investigate who pulled off the heist which almost killed him since the robbery/homicide cops seem unable to solve the crime. Leland; nice to see a man who values his dogs so fervently. The book flows to a believable and satisfying conclusion. I always enjoy Robert Crais's books and this one doesn't disappoint. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584186946i/29105834.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=cops-and-pee-eyes">cops-and-pee-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=all-fiction">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=miss-trees">miss-trees</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559028615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17191686204641794143">A man and his dog. It's a beautiful thing. <br/><br/>Maggie the German shepherd kicked this up into the five-star zone for me. Crais made her so real that I wanted to zip down to L.A. and stage a dognapping. Of a fictional dog...<br/><br/>Scott James is a Los Angeles cop with PTSD. Maggie has PTSD too, following an event in her service to the U.S. Marines. Scott and Maggie team up to solve a murder, and they end up rehabilitating each other. <br/><br/>I loved the way Crais included small sections viewed from the dog's perspe</span>
  <span id="freeText17191686204641794143" style="display:none">A man and his dog. It's a beautiful thing. <br /><br />Maggie the German shepherd kicked this up into the five-star zone for me. Crais made her so real that I wanted to zip down to L.A. and stage a dognapping. Of a fictional dog...<br /><br />Scott James is a Los Angeles cop with PTSD. Maggie has PTSD too, following an event in her service to the U.S. Marines. Scott and Maggie team up to solve a murder, and they end up rehabilitating each other. <br /><br />I loved the way Crais included small sections viewed from the dog's perspective. Not in any cheesy anthropomorphic way like certain dog books I won't mention. He just shows us how the dog sees with her nose and sorts out the various scents, and also how she finds her greatest joy in being part of a pack and serving the alpha, which in this case is Scott. <br /><br />My childhood dog was a female German shepherd. Maggie's priorities, and the way she behaves based on her interpretation of events, perfectly matched my memories of my dog. So much so that I was brought to tears a few times from missing my dog, even after almost 30 years without her. I even gained some new insights about my dog regarding things that wouldn't have crossed my mind when I was a youngster. <br /><br />And if you don't like dogs...well, this is still a good mystery. Crais is best known for his Elvis Cole and Joe Pike series, but this one is a stand-alone novel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17191686204641794143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_579088203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579088203" />
    <a title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh"><img alt="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346034704p2/10856439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579088203?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh" href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh">Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Admirer's of Working Dogs</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=indulge">indulge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579088203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1189660616017232255">This sounded great! About a working dog (don’t even get me started, I’m fanatical in my admiration) and a police officer both struggling with PTSD. Maggie the dog was a bomb sniffer in Afghanistan, Scott an LAPD cop. Both lost their partners, both are wounded - unable to function - that is till they meet and form a healing bond. Well written, the debilitating symptoms of PTSD described with finesse. <b>I mean what’s not to like? </b> An interesting touch Scott doesn’t even LIKE dogs, only chose a K-9 c</span>
  <span id="freeText1189660616017232255" style="display:none">This sounded great! About a working dog (don’t even get me started, I’m fanatical in my admiration) and a police officer both struggling with PTSD. Maggie the dog was a bomb sniffer in Afghanistan, Scott an LAPD cop. Both lost their partners, both are wounded - unable to function - that is till they meet and form a healing bond. Well written, the debilitating symptoms of PTSD described with finesse. <b>I mean what’s not to like? </b> An interesting touch Scott doesn’t even LIKE dogs, only chose a K-9 career because he couldn’t face losing another partner. The point of view by Maggie was handled well – didn’t find it corny, her focus on <i>preserving the pack </i>rang true. Add to that it’s written by a highly respected author I’ve been looking forward to trying out. <br /><b>So what went wrong?</b> Short on the police procedural department, the unraveling of his partner’s murder formula stuff, a satisfying but predictable outcome. The characters felt flat with the notable exception of the Sergeant in charge of the dog handling unit – he rocked. And while I knew it was coming I still wasn’t prepared – the bit where Maggie’s partner dies? Overdone, reeked of emotional manipulation. Okay – overreaction – I really need to grow up. Weaned on *Greyfriars Bobby, add to that personal experience with messed up abandoned dogs - any story about a dog unable to deal with losing their owner and I’m a puddle. <br />So not saying this isn’t worth reading because it is. A quick read, entertaining escapism, a solid 3 stars, I just expected a bit more. <br /><br /><i><b>"They will see and witness your greatest shame, and will not judge you! </b>These dogs will be the truest and best partners you can ever hope to have, and they will give their lives for you. And all they ask, all they want or need, all it costs YOU to get ALL of that, is a simple word of kindness." </i><br /><br /><b>*Greyfriars Bobby:</b> In 19th-century Edinburgh Bobby was a wee terrier famous for his unwavering devotion – legend has it he couldn’t be coaxed away from sleeping on the grave of his owner where he remained till the day he died. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1189660616017232255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_428058755" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/428058755" />
    <a title="Ami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/134600-ami"><img alt="Ami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485783876p2/134600.jpg" /></a>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16174358-suspect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=mystery-suspense-thriller">mystery-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=4-and-half-stars_rating">4-and-half-stars_rating</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428058755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10527192495678838710"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I gobbled this up for few hours -- safely to say that this is, so far, my <b>FAVORITE</b> Robert Crais novel, Cole/Pike notwithstanding.<br/><br/>For me personally, this novel is less on the thriller-suspense but more on the friendship between Scott and the amazing 85-pound black-and-tan German shepherd dog by the name of Maggie. Both Scott and Maggie have experienced a tragedy in their lives. <br/><br/>Scott got shot at the same night he lost his partner, Stephanie in a sudden nighttime assault. Scott always fee</span>
  <span id="freeText10527192495678838710" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>I gobbled this up for few hours -- safely to say that this is, so far, my <b>FAVORITE</b> Robert Crais novel, Cole/Pike notwithstanding.<br><br>For me personally, this novel is less on the thriller-suspense but more on the friendship between Scott and the amazing 85-pound black-and-tan German shepherd dog by the name of Maggie. Both Scott and Maggie have experienced a tragedy in their lives. <br><br>Scott got shot at the same night he lost his partner, Stephanie in a sudden nighttime assault. Scott always feels guilty because he thinks Stephanie's last thought was that of Scott leaving her in the moment of need (he didn't, he just crawled away to their police car to try to call for help). Meanwhile, Maggie also suffered from PTSD after her handler was killed by IED in Afghanistan, and she also got shot. Determined not to take medical retirement, Scott undergoes K9 training. On the day he is supposed to get K9 dog, Scott and Maggie find each other. They are both considered 'suspect' -- not right for the job. But Scott and Maggie prove everyone wrong. <br><br>It is such a wonderful story. Scott never considers himself a dog man, but he learns how to deal with Maggie, how to talk to her, how to love her. And Maggie learns about his new 'Alpha', his mood, his body language. They end up healing each other. The part where Scott breaks down and cry and hugs Maggie is simply heartbreaking. I love the chapters where Maggie is the narrator. Her thoughts are simple yet honest...<br><br>"<i>The threat was gone.<br>Crate safe.<br>Pack safe.<br>Alpha safe.<br>Her job was done."</i><br><br>My other favorite secondary character would be the K-9 Platoon Chief Trainer, Dominick Leland. He seems to love his dogs more than he likes people *lol*. <br><br>It's a near perfect read for me. My only complain would be -- because Scott is not a homicide detective, he is not fully involved in the investigation of his shooting. Which is why I think the suspense is rather lacking. The ending also feels a bit rushed.<br><br>Despite of that... I know that I can just reread several sections of this book over and over again.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393350ra/757307.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10527192495678838710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2798822435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798822435" />
    <a title="Antigone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22009196-antigone"><img alt="Antigone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383249021p2/22009196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798822435?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antigone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antigone" href="/user/show/22009196-antigone">Antigone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22009196-antigone?shelf=mystery-detective">mystery-detective</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798822435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer599705406462559863">Robert Crais is one of my favorite authors of crime fiction. His work is sharp, well-crafted and beautifully paced. His characters have weight, his dialogue's smart, and it certainly doesn't hurt that his stories take place in my neck of the woods, modern-day Los Angeles, or that very few of his plots include forays into the entertainment industry. Oh, he dipped a toe early on, but his interest didn't stick and I'm grateful for that. Grateful he chose, instead, to explore the grittier side of th</span>
  <span id="freeText599705406462559863" style="display:none">Robert Crais is one of my favorite authors of crime fiction. His work is sharp, well-crafted and beautifully paced. His characters have weight, his dialogue's smart, and it certainly doesn't hurt that his stories take place in my neck of the woods, modern-day Los Angeles, or that very few of his plots include forays into the entertainment industry. Oh, he dipped a toe early on, but his interest didn't stick and I'm grateful for that. Grateful he chose, instead, to explore the grittier side of the city - the South Central gangs, the Yakuza, the Russian mafia, illegal immigration, the feds, the LAPD, ex-cons, serial killers, the missing and the lost. There's plenty going on in this locale that will never make it to reality television. And while I could argue for days on end that, say, coyotes (the men who smuggle people across the border) have more realistic meat to them than any friend of a botox needle...well, who's going to listen? So let the world think L.A. is filled with ditzy ex-wives, celebrity psychics and preening real estate agents. Some know better, and Robert Crais is one of them.<br /><br />It took a lot for me to set a Crais novel off to the side; to pull it from contention and cast it atop my dusty someday pile. That he was introducing new characters was not the problem. He'd done that before. But now...well...a dog. Didn't really matter that it was going to be an LAPD K-9, it was still a gosh-darn dog. A big ol' dog somebody was going to put in danger. A dog that, get this, came back from Afghanistan with a case of canine PTSD. This was all sorts of troublesome to me. And so, you know, years passed.<br /><br />I wish I could say my soft heart hardened, but I'm losing hope that's <i>ever</i> going to happen. That's just about as unlikely as the halt in publication of Robert Crais books. Because he's still writing, and my reserve is stacking up. I decided I had to get on with this. And just about halfway through? It became pretty apparent how much of a ninny I'd been.<br /><br />The guy likes dogs. Really likes them. And gets them. And gets that ineffable, core-of-the-heart bond that develops between human and canine. I mean, he's got passages here written from the perspective of a <i>German shepherd</i>. Took some brass to lay that down. But it works. The whole thing works and then some. I wasn't sure anything was going to top Joe Pike in <i>L.A. Requiem</i> - which stands untouched in the field of modern crime for me. Yet this story comes awfully close. It's just that good.<br /><br />Which reminds me of something I'd been a fool to forget.<br /><br />Robert Crais is an author I can trust.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="599705406462559863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11412180744974021318" style="display:none">What can I say here other than...SCORE?   <span id="freeText5447032447762129363" style="display:none">My second Robert Crais book, and this was a very entertaining, enjoyable, exciting read.<br /><br />I am an animal lover, which helps with this book, I admire the work done with all dog trainers/handlers/soldiers/police, which is the base of this story.<br /><br />What a team, one man and his dog, or one policeman and his dog.<br /><br />You feel throughout this book the relationship grow and built between a dog recovering from injury and a policeman recovering from injury together.<br /><br />The tension stays at an even pace for two thirds of the book, and then bang in one chapter the story speeds up to a great last few chapters.<br /><br />The main characters were great, and I like the idea of the story from the different characters including the dog Maggie.<br /><br />A book that makes you smile at times and also worry wants going to happen !<br /><br />I am a softy and love happy endings, but does not always happen that way.<br /><br />A great stand alone novel and highly recommended.<br /><br />Now a group read book !<br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1004898876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004898876" />
    <a title="James Thane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane"><img alt="James Thane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513566p2/3483907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004898876?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Thane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Thane" href="/user/show/3483907-james-thane">James Thane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=robert-crais">robert-crais</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3483907-james-thane?shelf=best-book-with-an-animal-in-it-of-a">best-book-with-an-animal-in-it-of-a</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004898876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18031358321236906982">MWD Maggie T415 is an eighty-five pound black and tan German shepherd; she's also a Marine halfway through her second deployment in Afghanistan. With her handler, Pete Gibbs, she works as part of a patrol and explosives detection team. The two are devoted to each other and then one morning, while out on patrol, Maggie is sniffing out IEDs, when the unit comes under enemy fire. Pete is killed; Maggie is badly wounded and when they are choppered out together, Maggie is left with no one.<br/><br/>Scott James</span>
  <span id="freeText18031358321236906982" style="display:none">MWD Maggie T415 is an eighty-five pound black and tan German shepherd; she's also a Marine halfway through her second deployment in Afghanistan. With her handler, Pete Gibbs, she works as part of a patrol and explosives detection team. The two are devoted to each other and then one morning, while out on patrol, Maggie is sniffing out IEDs, when the unit comes under enemy fire. Pete is killed; Maggie is badly wounded and when they are choppered out together, Maggie is left with no one.<br /><br />Scott James is a patrolman on the LAPD. Late one night out of nowhere, he and his partner, Stephanie Anders, suddenly find themselves in the middle of a shooting war when a gang of masked men attacks a Bentley rolling down the street in front of them. Two victims in the Bentley are killed as is Stephanie Anders. Scott James is very badly wounded and the killers get away clean.<br /><br />Ten months later, Scott is back on the job, if only barely. He's in therapy, attempting to deal with the trauma that still haunts him and hoping to recover memories of that night, no matter how small, that might somehow jumpstart the investigation and lead to the men who killed his partner.<br /><br />Scott's goal in the LAPD had always been to join the elite SWAT team, but there's no chance of that now. Instead, he's assigned to the K-9 unit. After an initial training period, he'll be paired with a dog. His new "partner" is still to be determined, but while in training he bonds with Maggie who has now mostly recovered from her physical wounds and is being retrained to work as a police dog.<br /><br />Both Scott and Maggie still bear the scars, physical and mental, of their traumatic experiences. The sergeant who leads the training unit doesn't have much faith either man or beast, but reluctantly agrees to give them a couple of weeks to prove themselves.<br /><br />In the meantime, Scott has managed to insert himself into the ongoing investigation of the crime that took his first partner's life. In therapy, he remembers a small but vital clue that reinvigorates the investigation and from that point the story progresses as we watch the progress of the investigation and the developing relationship between Maggie and Scott.<br /><br />It's a terrific story, which will come as no surprise to people who have read earlier books by Robert Crais. But what is astounding is the development of Maggie, who becomes perhaps the book's central character. Certainly, she's the most intriguing character and at several points, the story unfolds from her point of view. It sounds sappy, but Crais makes it work brilliantly. <br /><br />This is not, by any stretch of the imagination, one of those dopey books where dogs and cats think like human beings and are almost always smarter than most of the humans in the book. Maggie thinks like a dog, and she's totally believable; her role in the story requires not the slightest suspension of disbelief. She's one of the most unique and interesting characters to come along in crime fiction in a long time, and we can only hope that this won't be the last time we see her.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18031358321236906982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_491915717" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491915717" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/491915717?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">animal lovers, crime fiction lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=police-federal-agent-law-enforcemen">police-federal-agent-law-enforcemen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=animal-character-steals-the-show">animal-character-steals-the-show</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=nursed-back-to-health">nursed-back-to-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=character-grieving-loved-one">character-grieving-loved-one</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer491915717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6832238254708838156">This is a book that you need to read if you're an animal lover! I loved the whole aspect of the bond that formed between Scott and Maggie. They are both wounded warriors, grieving their lost love ones, and somewhat rejected because of their emotional/physical wounds. Maggie was so awesome, I felt my heart fill with love for this wonderful German Shepherd. I am a huge fan of this breed, and Crais presents their wonderful natures in the most truthful and vibrant way. <br/><br/>Crais fills in some interestin</span>
  <span id="freeText6832238254708838156" style="display:none">This is a book that you need to read if you're an animal lover! I loved the whole aspect of the bond that formed between Scott and Maggie. They are both wounded warriors, grieving their lost love ones, and somewhat rejected because of their emotional/physical wounds. Maggie was so awesome, I felt my heart fill with love for this wonderful German Shepherd. I am a huge fan of this breed, and Crais presents their wonderful natures in the most truthful and vibrant way. <br /><br />Crais fills in some interesting tidbits on the training of police dogs and their holders and what military dogs do. That aspect of Maggie in the frontlines with her handler just about tore my heart out. I cheer on military people who do that important and dangerous job, and it squeezes my heart as an animal lover how equally dangerous it is for their working dogs. Police dogs also serve a crucial role and they can face some very dangerous situations in the line of duty. Scott's boss reminded me of my dad who was a country boy who loved dogs. He had his down to earth manner and sense of connection to dogs that was almost spiritual.<br /><br />Scott is a good character, but honestly, I needed more of his inner world. I feel that this was a function of this book being too short. I would have liked a longer, more expansive story that took place over a longer time period. While the bond between Scott and Maggie totally sells this book, I would have found it more believable had it taken place over a longer period of time. Such as it was, I loved it. Maggie is such a wonderful companion, and I liked that not only does she help Scott heal, he helps her as well. While I am a cat lady, I also love dogs, and this book made me long to bring home my very own German Shepherd Dog one day soon. Crais shows how important the human animal bond is in society and how therapeutic animals and people can be to each other. Sorry to go on my soapbox. I can't help it because this book really touches on this issue which is so dear to my heart. <br /><br />The mystery part felt undeveloped, honestly. Crais is an excellent mystery writer, so I don't mean to put him down, but it was a bit simplistic compared to some of his other works. I was surprised at the culprits and the look Ta police corruption is sobering. The secondary characters add texture to the story, but some of their parts felt under-represented.<br /><br />Man, I hate to put this book down in my review! I have so much love for the whole aspect of Maggie and Scott as partners, and I am truly in love with Maggie. She's up there with Einstein from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32423.Watchers" title="Watchers by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Watchers</a> for me, which is really saying something. This book has something so powerful to say about the love between people and their pets/animals that it earns a special place in my heart. And honestly, I still feel it deserves four stars despite some of my issues with its brevity affecting the execution of the overall storyline.<br /><br />Definitely check this out. The audiobook is really good and the narrator is excellent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6832238254708838156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14083368204381358749" style="display:none">Great pacing, straightforward, good prose style, and detailed enough to be satisfying.<br><br>This is mostly a "classic" detective story, uncovering clues and knitting a big picture of a crime in linear fashion.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441878572" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441878572?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2015</a>

  <span id="freeText8892469443531708121" style="display:none">Eight months after being horrifically injured in an armed hold up in which his partner dies, LAPD cop Scott James is trying to get on with his life and is training to be a K-9 police dog handler. Not really a dog lover, something clicks when he meets Maggie the German shepherd, herself badly injured in Afghanistan when her army handler was killed. <br /><br />Together Scott and Maggie start to form a bond and become a formidable team especially when Scott starts to look into why little progress has been made investigating the armed holdup that left him for dead. <br /><br />This is a delightful story with the author allowing Maggie some chapters to show us her view of the events and her strong bond with Scott and bravery in trying to protect him against all odds. </span>

<div id="review_909407817" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909407817" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/909407817?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer909407817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1296821548875374364">I heard Robert Crais talk about his book <u>Suspect</u> a while ago. I was immediately attracted to the story by Crais' enthusiasm for his subject. Many authors are dog owners, some host to a houseful. I thought Crais was one of them. Reading his bio I see his home is a feline one at present but I knew there had to be dogs in his past. Reading additional interviews Crais explains he had always had dogs from the time he was a kid. The last, Yoshi, was a big guy, an Akita. After living with Crais for fif</span>
  <span id="freeText1296821548875374364" style="display:none">I heard Robert Crais talk about his book <u>Suspect</u> a while ago. I was immediately attracted to the story by Crais' enthusiasm for his subject. Many authors are dog owners, some host to a houseful. I thought Crais was one of them. Reading his bio I see his home is a feline one at present but I knew there had to be dogs in his past. Reading additional interviews Crais explains he had always had dogs from the time he was a kid. The last, Yoshi, was a big guy, an Akita. After living with Crais for fifteen years, Yoshi died in Crais' arms. Since Yoshi's death he has been unable to bring himself to choose another dog. He chalks this up to a feeling of disloyalty and yet he has always been interested in the dog-man relationship. This is apparent in <u>Suspect</u>. Craig dedicates <u>Suspect</u> to Gregg Hurwitz.<br /><br /> <i>for Gregg Hurwitz, friend, dog man, writer, and his beautiful pack: Delinah, Rosie, Natalie, and Simba.</i><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The first chapter is a grabber as we learn how Maggie, a German Shepard military dog is injured while working with her partner Pete. They are a pack of two. It is a gut wrenching and heartbreaking scene as we see Maggie protecting and covering Pete with her body when they are ambushed by an IED. When the helicopter lands to give Pete and Maggie aide, she won't let anyone near Pete. They are a pack. Maggie snarls and growls, ready to tear anyone coming near Pete apart. Finally the men are able to get Maggie into the helicopter and tell the pilot:<br /><br /> <i>"Stop talking' and fly motherfucker. You get her to a doctor. This dog's a marine."</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Scott James, an LAPD Cop loses his partner Stephanie one night when they are ambushed in a shoot-out while on patrol. Scott life is hanging by a thread. Eight months later he finds himself back on the job and assigned to the K-9 forces. On the day he is to be assigned his dog, he comes across Maggie, seemingly unfit for K-9 duty. Scott feels an instant camaraderie with Maggie and gets Dominick Leland, the head dog trainer to give he and Maggie a chance. Leland's take on Scott and Maggie is telling:<br /><br /> <i>That poor animal is unfit for this job, and I suspect the same about him. I hope to God in His Glory I am wrong, sincerely I do, but there it is. They are suspect.</i><br /><br />I don't have any dogs but thoroughly enjoyed learning about the training and bonding of these two broken spirits. I think <u>Suspect</u> was written as a stand-alone but it soon became apparent that fans of the book wanted more of this team, this pack of two. <u>The Promise</u> an Elvis Cole and Joe Pike novel due to be published in November 2014 will see the return of Scott James and his K-9 partner Maggie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1296821548875374364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16343387557743145514">4/5; 4 stars; A-<br/><br/>MacLeod Andrews did a good job narrating this audiobook. I think its always especially challenging to tell a story where part of the viewpoint is taken from that of an animal. I think the portrayal of the dog training/dog behaviour information in this book brought it from a 3 star to 4 star rating for me. The spotlight really shone on Maggie and what an extraordinary soldier she was. The training these working dogs and their handlers undergo is intensive and detailed. I think the</span>
  <span id="freeText16343387557743145514" style="display:none">4/5; 4 stars; A-<br /><br />MacLeod Andrews did a good job narrating this audiobook. I think its always especially challenging to tell a story where part of the viewpoint is taken from that of an animal. I think the portrayal of the dog training/dog behaviour information in this book brought it from a 3 star to 4 star rating for me. The spotlight really shone on Maggie and what an extraordinary soldier she was. The training these working dogs and their handlers undergo is intensive and detailed. I think the book did that justice. The police mystery was pretty good it was overshadowed by the human/dog interaction. <br /><br />One niggle, I find it hard to believe that an officer, so close to being pushed out after physical and mental trauma would be allowed so much latitude in his work. He was basically a wild card.<br /><br /></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15271523051271328673">Truly Outstanding. One of Crais' best. On a par with Taken and The Watchman. If you are a dog person you will know exactly what is going on. If you are a cat person you will learn a lot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1494667606221838635" style="display:none"><br>I loved this Robert Crais's novel. So much that I pre-ordered his next book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22172425.The_Promise__Elvis_Cole__14__Joe_Pike__5_" title="The Promise (Elvis Cole #14; Joe Pike #5) by Robert Crais" rel="nofollow noopener">The Promise</a>), due out April 28. Therefore, his participation in the investigation that takes place in this novel is more that of a private detective than of an active police officer. As for Pike, basically, it's a big two-legged dog. Pike is not a speaker, he is a doer, especially when things go bad. He is always ready to attack the enemy and save his friend, just as Maggie, the dog of war in Suspect.<br><br>Do not jump to the wrong conclusion. I looove Pike! And I loved Maggie.<br><br>Suspect keeps the readers on the edge of their seats from prologue to end. Some parts are even the kind that prompts us to bite our nails. I also liked the chapters that present what's happening from Maggie's point of view.<br><br>Crais is definitely one of the world's best thriller writers. My love for his work remains strong.<br></span>

        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/31175766-kathy">Kathy</a>

But...there is war action and then crime action in LA as well.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1739411799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1739411799" />
    <a title="D.G." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/210123-d-g"><img alt="D.G." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330353755p2/210123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1739411799?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="D.G." class="user" itemprop="url" name="D.G." href="/user/show/210123-d-g">D.G.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425278277" href="/book/show/21413818-suspect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=awesome-narration">awesome-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=picked-because-narrator">picked-because-narrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=macleod-andrews">macleod-andrews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1739411799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2122858643614460038">Way to make me tear up in the prologue.<br/><br/>I bought Suspect just because MacLeod Andrews is the narrator. I hadn’t even remembered that I had read a previous book by this author (The Two Minute Rule) so I had no expectations besides the excellent narration. But in the prologue, we see Maggie’s POV (yes, the dog has a POV!) from the time when she lost her handler. And I was hooked.<br/><br/>And in love.<br/><br/>With the dog.<br/><br/>And I’m not even a dog person!<br/><br/>Like Maggie, Scott also lost his partner to violence and 9 months </span>
  <span id="freeText2122858643614460038" style="display:none">Way to make me tear up in the prologue.<br /><br />I bought Suspect just because MacLeod Andrews is the narrator. I hadn’t even remembered that I had read a previous book by this author (The Two Minute Rule) so I had no expectations besides the excellent narration. But in the prologue, we see Maggie’s POV (yes, the dog has a POV!) from the time when she lost her handler. And I was hooked.<br /><br />And in love.<br /><br />With the dog.<br /><br />And I’m not even a dog person!<br /><br />Like Maggie, Scott also lost his partner to violence and 9 months later, the culprits haven’t been apprehended. Scott’s life has changed dramatically since the shooting: he’s in pain, traumatized, and stubbornly refusing to take a medical retirement. It’s not clear why Scott decides to go for the K-9 unit but once he does, his and Maggie’s path intersect.<br /><br />Maggie’s life has also changed since she lost her partner. Loud noises startle her and she’s timid around people. Understandably, Sgt. Leland (Scott’s boss) thinks she’s not fit for duty but once Scott learns of her situation (so much like his!), he asks Leland to give them a chance. Leland for his part, thinks Scott should have retired and sees this as a way to kill two birds with one stone. If Scott fails (as he’s bound to do), then maybe Scott will realize this job is not for him.<br /><br />But he doesn’t count on Scott’s drive and stubbornness. Slowly, he begins to bond with Maggie, even talking to his own shrink to find out how to help with her PTSD. At the same time, Scott gets involved in the investigation about his shooting, now that new detectives are on the case. This was the weak part of the book. After I remembered The Two Minute Rule, I realized the plots were very similar. Same bad guys, same motive. The way in which Scott found the witness seemed too convoluted (although I understand this was a way to involve Maggie) and how he became a “suspect” was so fishy that you wonder how the Police was taken in. I liked Maggie and Scott so much though that I just went along for the ride.<br /><br />Scott is a really nice guy. He carries a lot of guilt about the shooting – he can’t forget Stephanie’s last words – and he feels like he let her down. There’s a sense of sadness and regret about what could have been (which was also similar to the MC from the The Two Minute Rule) but there’s also the determination to do right by his partner this time around.<br /><br />I loved how the author did Maggie’s POV. Her thoughts are all about pleasing and protecting Scott, who after a time, she considers her Alpha. With Scott, she’s all sweetness but when she’s on the job, she all business. She’s constantly evaluating threats and totally fierce when Scott is in danger. Her favorite mantra is: “Scott safe. Maggie safe. Pack safe.” She’s so precious! (I told you I’m in love.:)<br /><br />As usual, MacLeod Andrews rocked the narration. His voices are great, his pacing is just right (I speed up most narrators but not him!) He’s one of the few narrators that can do both YA and Adult equally well…and he’s cute to boot! (Yes, I’ve googled him…don’t judge me.)<br /><br />Overall, I think any mystery reader will enjoy this book but for animal lovers, it will be a definite treat.<br /><br /><i>Review of audiobook version narrated by MacLeod Andrews, first posted at <a href="www.badassbookreviews.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Badass Book Reviews. </a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2122858643614460038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_540495277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540495277" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5537205-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505620458p2/5537205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540495277?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/5537205-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540495277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8807841920514428771">SUSPECT had all the makings of a good novel, at least on paper anyway: well-rounded characters, intriguing plot, subplots, and interesting twists along the way. But I can’t help but think it was like kissing your sister. Sure, you can grin and bear it and hold back the gag reflex and then immediately drink a bottle of Scope, but there’s no spark, no flare. The moment ends and then you end up racing off in the other direction and having nightmares for weeks.<br/><br/>Maggie certainly had plenty of chutzpah</span>
  <span id="freeText8807841920514428771" style="display:none">SUSPECT had all the makings of a good novel, at least on paper anyway: well-rounded characters, intriguing plot, subplots, and interesting twists along the way. But I can’t help but think it was like kissing your sister. Sure, you can grin and bear it and hold back the gag reflex and then immediately drink a bottle of Scope, but there’s no spark, no flare. The moment ends and then you end up racing off in the other direction and having nightmares for weeks.<br /><br />Maggie certainly had plenty of chutzpah, and her handlers Scott and Pete weren’t too bad themselves, but this novel seemed to skim over the surface, the way a good oil cleanup operation is supposed to work. The mystery proved interesting enough, but I missed the thrills along the way. I certainly didn’t have a burning need to race toward the end, sacrificing sleep, extraneous thoughts, bathroom breaks, and the basic necessities of life.<br /><br />In fact, what drove me more than anything to finish this novel was my desire to return it to my friend. Otherwise, the end would have been delayed, as I discovered a read that grabbed me by the wrist and pulled me forward. That’s not to say this isn’t well-written. Because it certainly is. I just had to drag my left leg across the finish line.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8807841920514428771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

I was recommended this book by a fellow dog lover and I just love-love-love Maggie, and the fact some of the chapters are written from her point-of-view. Gives a realistic depiction of PTSD. This is a great thriller that you'll have a hard time putting down.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pvLWthrcpwuGjdFqmskmfzDdmN3RpvqlAXl9pVs7EHL3ZjUPHkSo3Nfq8XRDECxBhq8VBfwN0QY8tpp8vKhV6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

But his inquiry hits a snag when he himself becomes a suspect.\n\nAs he races to clear his name, McEvoy\'s findings point to a serial killer working under the radar of law enforcement for years, and using personal data shared by the victims themselves to select and hunt his targets.\n\nCalled &quot;the Raymond Chandler of this generation&quot; (Associated Press), Michael Connelly once again This time around the two detectives are joined by LAPD K-9 Officer Scott James and his K-9 partner, German shepherd Maggie, from another Crais’ stand-alone novel, Suspect. The collaboration of both crime-solving teams is Crais’ attempt to bring different motivations and perspectives into the same case with the intention of adding depth to the investigation. Although a great idea in theory, it quickly becomes a small stage with too many large players to allow the partnership to reach its full potential. With a cast of characters accustomed to owning the spotlight, none of them get the opportunity to truly shine in a satisfactory way. Readers who are familiar with them from previous novels will find they lack depth and personality in this novel as they simply carry out the roles handed to them with very little fanfare.  Private detective Elvis Cole thinks he is just taking on another missing person’s case when he agrees to search for Amy Breslyn. When his first lead sends to him a house filled with explosives and a dead body, he realizes there is more to his client’s story than he anticipated. His presence in the neighborhood that night earns him the role of possible murder suspect and he finds himself on the receiving end of police surveillance while he tries to conduct his own investigation under the radar.  This companion includes the following: • Book Review • Story Setting Analysis • Story elements you may have missed as we decipher the novel • Summary of the text, with some analytical comments interspersed • Thought Provoking /or Discussion Questions for both Readers &amp; Book Clubs • Discussion &amp; Analysis of Themes, Symbols… • And Much More!       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8944.Robert_Crais">About Robert Crais</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8944.Robert_Crais"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1202587973p3/8944.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8944.Robert_Crais">Robert Crais
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,428
followers
</div>

</div>
